Refine by binary search\n            t_left = t_coarse[idx]\n            t_right = t_coarse[idx+1]\n            for _ in range(30):\n                t_mid = (t_left + t_right) / 2\n                # Compute left and right derivative approximations\n                eps = 1e-6 * max(1.0, abs(t_mid))\n                f_plus = forward(e_j * (t_mid + eps))\n                f_minus = forward(e_j * (t_mid - eps))\n                deriv_mid = (f_plus - f_minus) / (2 * eps)\n                \n                f_plus2 = forward(e_j * (t_mid + 2*eps))\n                f_minus2 = forward(e_j * (t_mid - 2*eps))\n                deriv2 = (f_plus2 - f_minus2) / (4*eps)\n                \n                # Since we don't know which neuron, just refine based on the approximate location\n                # Use the fact that around a breakpoint, the left and right slopes differ\n                # The change in slope happens at t_i = -b1[i]/A1[i,j]\n                # We can approximate by checking f''(t) via central difference\n                \n                f_m2 = forward(e_j * (t_mid - 2*eps))\n                f_m1 = forward(e_j * (t_mid - eps))\n                f_p1 = forward(e_j * (t_mid + eps))\n                f_p2 = forward(e_j * (t_mid + 2*eps))\n                \n                # Actually, better: compute slope at points straddling the breakpoint\n            eps1 = 1e-5 * max(1.0, abs(refined_t))\n            f_t_eps1 = forward(e_j * (refined_t - eps1))\n            f_t = forward(e_j * refined_t)\n            f_t_eps2 = forward(e_j * (refined_t + eps1))\n            \n            slope_before = (f_t - f_t_eps1) / eps1\n            slope_after = (f_t_eps2 - f_t) / eps1\n            \n            slope_change_final = slope_after - slope_before\n            \n            breakpoints.append((refined_t, slope_change_final))\n        \n        # Identify unique neurons by clustering on |t*Δ|\n    # Use the fact that there should be 20 groups\n    inv_values = np.array([abs(inv) for _, _, _, inv in all_bps])\n    \n    # Simple clustering: sort and find gaps\n    if len(inv_values) == 0:\n        print(\"No breakpoints found!\")\n        return None\n    \n    sorted_idx = np.argsort(inv_values)\n    sorted_vals = inv_values[sorted_idx]\n    \n    # Find large gaps between consecutive values\n    gaps = np.diff(sorted_vals)\n    # We expect 20 neurons, so look for breaks\n    gap_threshold = np.percentile(gaps, 80)  # top 20% gaps are likely between clusters\n    break_indices = [0]\n    for i in range(len(gaps)):\n        if gaps[i] > max(gap_threshold, 1e-7):\n            break_indices.append(i + 1)\n    break_indices.append(len(sorted_vals))\n    \n    clusters = []\n    for k in range(len(break_indices) - 1):\n        start, end = break_indices[k], break_indices[k+1]\n        if end - start >= 3:  #
